:3. Find the number of natural numbers k, not exceeding 267000, such that k^{2}-1 is divisible by 267. Answer: 4000.

:Let triangle XYZ be a triangle with sides of length x, y and z, and suppose this triangle is acute (so all [altitudes](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Altitude) are in the interior of the triangle).Let the altitude to the side of length x be of length h_x, and similarly for y and z. Then we have by two applications of the [Pythagorean Theorem](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Pythagorean_Theorem) we that [x = sqrt{y^2 - h_x^2} + sqrt{z^2 - h_x^2}] As a [function](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Function) of h_x, the [RHS](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php?title=RHS&action=edit&redlink=1) of this equation is strictly decreasing, so it takes each value in its [range](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Range) exactly once. Thus we must have that h_x^2 = frac1{16} and so h_x = frac{1}4 and similarly h_y = frac15 and h_z = frac16.The area of the triangle must be the same no matter how we measure it; therefore xcdot h_x = ycdot h_y = z cdot h_z gives us frac x4 = frac y5 = frac z6 = 2A and x = 8A, y = 10A and z = 12A. The [semiperimeter](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Semiperimeter) of the triangle is s = frac{8A + 10A + 12A}{2} = 15A so by [Heron's formula](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Heron%27s_formula) we have [A = sqrt{15A cdot 7A cdot 5A cdot 3A} = 15A^2sqrt{7}]Thus, A = frac{1}{15sqrt{7}} and x + y + z = 30A = frac2{sqrt{7}} and the answer is 2 + 7 = boxed{009}.The justification that there is an acute triangle with sides of length x, y and z:Note that x, y and z are each the sum of two positive [square roots](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Square_root) of real numbers, so x, y, z geq 0. (Recall that, by [AIME](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/AIME) [ convention](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Mathematical_convention), all numbers (including square roots) are taken to be real unless otherwise indicated.) Also, sqrt{y^2-frac{1}{16}} < sqrt{y^2} = y, so we have x < y + z, y < z + x and z < x + y. But these conditions are exactly those of the [triangle inequality](https://artofproblemsolving.com/wiki/index.php/Triangle_inequality), so there does exist such a triangle.

:Problem 5. Determine the angles in the isosceles triangle ABC, in which the height dropped to the base is half the length of the angle bisector of one of the angles at the base.

:[<think>Okay, so I need to find the angles of an isosceles triangle ABC where the height dropped to the base is half the length of the angle bisector of one of the angles at the base. Hmm, let me start by visualizing the triangle. Since it's isosceles, two sides are equal. Let's assume that AB and AC are the equal sides, so the base is BC. The height dropped from A to BC will split the base into two equal parts. Let me denote the height as h, and the angle bisector from one of the base angles, say angle B, as l. The problem states that h = (1/2)l. First, let me recall some formulas. In an isosceles triangle, the height h can be related to the sides. If we let the equal sides be length c, and the base be length b, then the height h can be calculated using Pythagoras: h = sqrt(c - (b/2)). For the angle bisector, there's a formula for the length of an angle bisector in a triangle. The angle bisector from angle B will split the opposite side (AC in this case) into segments proportional to the adjacent sides. Wait, but in our triangle, since AB = AC = c, the angle bisector from angle B (which is at vertex B) will go to some point on AC. Let me make sure I recall the angle bisector theorem correctly. The theorem states that the angle bisector divides the opposite side into segments proportional to the adjacent sides. So, in triangle ABC, if we have an angle bisector from B to AC, then the point D where the bisector meets AC divides AC into segments AD and DC such that AD/DC = AB/BC. But AB = c, and BC = b. Identify the angles and sides: - Let the base angles be (beta) and the vertex angle be (alpha). - Since the triangle is isosceles, (alpha + 2beta = 180^circ).2. Express the height and angle bisector: - The height (h) from (A) to (BC) is (h = x sin beta), where (x) is the length of (AB) and (AC). - The angle bisector (BD) from (B) to (AC) can be expressed using trigonometric identities and Stewart's theorem.3. Relate the height and angle bisector: - The problem states (h = frac{1}{2} BD). - Using the formula for the angle bisector length and trigonometric identities, we derive the equation: [ sin beta = frac{2 cos beta cos(beta/2)}{1 + 2 cos beta} ]4. Solve the trigonometric equation: - Simplifying the equation leads to (sin(3beta/2) = cos beta). - Solving this, we find (beta = 36^circ).5. Determine the vertex angle: - The vertex angle (alpha = 180^circ - 2beta = 180^circ - 72^circ = 108^circ).Thus, the angles of triangle (ABC) are (boxed{36^circ}), (boxed{36^circ}), and (boxed{108^circ}).]

First, we use the principle of inclusion-exclusion to find the overlap between swimming and soccer:[text{Total students} = text{Swim} + text{Soccer} - text{Both}][33 = 22 + 22 - text{Both} implies text{Both} = 11]Thus, 11 students participate in both activities, leaving 11 students who swim only and 11 who play soccer only each day.Next, we consider the transitions between activities from yesterday to today. For today's soccer players (22 students), 15 swam yesterday and 15 played soccer yesterday. Using inclusion-exclusion:[15 + 15 - 22 = 8 implies 8 text{ students did both yesterday}]This leaves 7 students who swam only yesterday and 7 who played soccer only yesterday. Similarly, the same applies to today's swimmers.We model the transitions using the following variables:- (a): students who swam only yesterday.- (b): students who played soccer only yesterday.- (c): students who did both yesterday.Each day, the number of students in each category is 11 swim only, 11 soccer only, and 11 both. The transitions are:- From swim only yesterday (11 students): 4 stay swim only, 4 switch to soccer only, 3 switch to both.- From soccer only yesterday (11 students): 4 stay soccer only, 4 switch to swim only, 3 switch to both.- From both yesterday (11 students): 3 switch to swim only, 3 switch to soccer only, 5 stay both.Thus, the number of students who stayed in swim only from yesterday to today is 4. The match stops when the score difference is 2 or after 6 games have been played. The key steps are as follows:1. Base Cases: - If (|d| geq 2), the match stops, so (E(d, n) = 0). - If (n = 6), the match stops, so (E(d, 6) = 0).2. The probability of player A winning each game is (frac{2}{3}) and player B winning is (frac{1}{3}).We define (E(t, d)) as the expected number of games remaining from time (t) with a score difference (d). The key steps are as follows:1. Base Cases: - If the score difference (|d| geq 2), the match stops, so (E(t, d) = 0). - If (t = 6), the match stops regardless of the score, so (E(6, d) = 0).2. Recursive Relations: - For other states, the expected number of games is computed as: [ E(t, d) = 1 + frac{2}{3}E(t+1, d+1) + frac{1}{3}E(t+1, d-1) ]3. Calculations: - At (t = 5): - (E(5, +1) = 1) and (E(5, -1) = 1) because the game ends at (t = 6). - At (t = 4): - (E(4, 0) = 1 + frac{2}{3}E(5, +1) + frac{1}{3}E(5, -1) = 2) - At (t = 3): - (E(3, +1) = 1 + frac{2}{3} cdot 0 + frac{1}{3} cdot 2 = frac{5}{3}) - (E(3, -1) = 1 + frac{2}{3} cdot 2 + frac{1}{3} cdot 0 = frac{7}{3}) - At (t = 2): - (E(2, 0) = 1 + frac{2}{3} cdot frac{5}{3} + frac{1}{3} cdot frac{7}{3} = frac{26}{9}) - At (t = 1): - (E(1, +1) = 1 + frac{1}{3} cdot frac{26}{9} = frac{53}{27}) - (E(1, -1) = 1 + frac{2}{3} cdot frac{26}{9} = frac{79}{27}) - At (t = 0): - (E(0, 0) = 1 + frac{2}{3} cdot frac{53}{27} + frac{1}{3} cdot frac{79}{27} = frac{266}{81})Thus, the expected number of games played when the match stops is (boxed{B}).]

:3. B.According to the problem, all possible values of xi are 2, 4, 6.Let each two games be a round. Then the probability that the match stops at the end of this round is left(frac{2}{3}right)^{2}+left(frac{1}{3}right)^{2}=frac{5}{9}.If the match continues after this round, then A and B must each have scored 1 point in this round, and the result of this round has no impact on whether the match stops in the next round. Therefore,begin{array}{l}P(xi=2)=frac{5}{9}, P(xi=4)=frac{4}{9} times frac{5}{9}=frac{20}{81}, P(xi=6)=left(frac{4}{9}right)^{2}=frac{16}{81} .end{array}Thus, E xi=2 times frac{5}{9}+4 times frac{20}{81}+6 times frac{16}{81}=frac{266}{81}.
